## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical reaction kinetics, specifically modeling the temporal evolution of a reactant concentration. The rate of change dA_dt typically depends on the instantaneous concentration A via power-law or autocatalytic mechanisms, and may incorporate time-dependent effects like catalyst deactivation or non-isothermal conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- General power-law kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (standard n-th order reaction rate)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-accelerated mechanism)
- Linear relaxation: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to equilibrium concentration)
- Competing pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 - c1 * A (parallel second-order formation and first-order decay)
- Time-modulated kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (varying catalyst activity or non-isothermal condition)
- Chain propagation: dA_dt = c0 * A * log(c1 * A) (radical polymerization or branching kinetics)
- Source-sink balance: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (zero-order input with linear removal)
- Diffusion-limited surface reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**(1/2) (transport-controlled erosion or film growth)
- Catalyst deactivation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * t) (time-dependent activity loss)
- Steric hindrance rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(-c1 * A) (active site blocking at high concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass action principle → Product of concentration terms raised to stoichiometric powers (A**n)
- Catalyst deactivation → Multiplicative time-dependent decay factor exp(-c*t) or (1+c*t)**(-1) scaling the rate
- Autocatalytic acceleration → Non-monotonic rate peaking at intermediate concentrations, structured as A*(c-A)
- Diffusion vs reaction control → Transition from integer reaction orders to fractional powers (e.g., A**0.5) indicating transport limitations
- Competing reaction pathways → Difference of distinct kinetic terms representing parallel or consecutive steps
- Induction/lag phase → Initial rate suppression that recovers, often modeled via time-modulated factors or delayed activation
- Chain branching/termination → Logarithmic or exponential concentration dependence in radical/polymerization kinetics
- Steady-state relaxation → Rate approaches zero linearly or exponentially as concentration nears equilibrium value

### Analysis of Candidates

The Ground Truth (GT) function is:
`GT = -k1*A - k2*A*exp(-k3*t) + k4*sin(log(A + 1))`
where `k1, k2, k3, k4` are fixed positive constants derived from the provided numerical values. The essential basis functions required for an exact match are:
1. `A` (linear in A)
2. `A * exp(c * t)` (product of A and exponential of t)
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` (sine of the natural logarithm of A+1)

Any candidate lacking the `sin(log(A + 1))` term cannot be algebraically equivalent to the GT, as trigonometric and logarithmic/exponential functions are linearly independent. We will evaluate each candidate based on this structural requirement.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

This has three terms:
1. A linear term in A: `-0.25667*A`
2. An exponential decay term: `-0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t)`
3. A sin(log(A+1)) term: `0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

The key basis functions are: `A`, `A*exp(c*t)`, and `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(log(A+1))` or equivalent. Most candidates use `log(A*c + 1)` or `exp(A*c)` terms but NOT `sin(log(...))`. Only candidates 19 and 20 contain `sin(log(A + 1))`.

This is exactly the form: `c0*A + c1*A*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(log(A+1))`. Setting c0 = -0.25667, c1 = -0.25667, c2 = -0.02054, c3 = 0.94264 gives exact match.

**Candidate 20:** `A*(c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)) + c3*sin(log(A + 1))`

Expanding: `c0*A + c1*A*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(log(A+1))`. This is identical to Candidate 19.

Candidate 20 verdict: [MATCH]

For all other candidates (1-18, 21-50), none contain `sin(log(...))`.
